Jamison Brereton

63 (889)
All Gods
Gaya Pl─Бta
17 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 16тАУ17
The signature word of this hymn is svast├н тАЬwell-beingтАЭ: in the dative suvast├бye it provides the last four syllables of verses 3тАУ14, and its nominative opens five consecutive p─Бdas in the verses after that refrain (15тАУ16a). The gods from whom the poet solicits well-being are primarily the ─Аdityas and their mother Aditi, who especially dominate the first half of the hymn. Beginning with verse 9 other gods are also invoked, though the ─Аdityas keep their prominence. Not surprisingly in a hymn devoted to well-being, the emphasis is on positive thoughts, though some worries about potential dangers do intrude (see vss. 11тАУ12). More surprisingly in a hymn with such a strong ─Аdityan cast, our potential moral flaws are barely men
tioned (vs. 8c).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the gods who, (coming) from afar proclaim their affinity (with men), and beloved by men, (support)the genitive rations of (Manu, the son of) Vivasvat; may they who are seated on the sacred grass of Yay─Бti, the sonof Nahuс╣гa, speak favourably unto us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those from afar who seek to establish friendship, who, gratified by Manu, (seek to establish) the races of Vivasvant,
the gods who sit on the ritual grass of Yay─Бti Nahuс╣гyaтАФlet them speak on our behalf.

Griffith

MAY they who would assume kinship from far away, Vivasvan’s generations, dearly loved of men,
Even the Gods who sit upon the sacred grass of Nahusa’s son Yayati, bless and comfort us.

Geldner

Die von ferne Freundschaft schlie├Яen m├╢chten und von Manu zufriedengestellt zu des Vivasvat Geschlecht kommen, die auf dem Barhis des Yayati, des Nahusohnes, sitzen, die G├╢tter sollen unsere F├╝rsprecher sein.

Grassmann

Die gern von ferne kommen zur Genossenschaft, geliebt von Menschen, des Vivasvat hoher Stamm, Die auf der Streu Jajati’s Sohns des Nahuscha als G├╢tter sitzen, m├╢gen tr├╢stend uns erfreun.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll your appellations, gods, are to be revered and praised, and worshipped, and whether you aresprung from heaven, or from the firmament, or from earth, hear at this (solemnity) my invocation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Appellations:n─Бm─Бni = ┼Ыar─лr─Бс╣Зi, bodies or forms

Jamison Brereton

For all your names, o gods, are worthy of homage, worthy of praise, and they are worthy of the sacrifice.
You who were born from Aditi or from the waters, who from the earth, listen to my call here.

Griffith

For worthy of obeisance, Gods, are all your names, worthy of adoration and of sacrifice.
Ye who were born from waters, and from Aditi, and from the earth, do ye here listen to my call.

Geldner

Denn alle eure Namen sind ehrw├╝rdig, lobw├╝rdig, ihr G├╢tter, und anbetungswert. Die ihr von der Aditi abstammet, vom Wasser, die ihr von der Erde, erh├╢ret hier meinen Ruf!

Grassmann

Denn alle eure Namen, o ihr G├╢tter, sind des Betens, der Verehrung und des Opfers werth; Die aus dem Himmel, aus der Erd’, aus Wassern ihr geboren seid, vernehmet hier nun meinen Ruf.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo (these dieties) to whom the maternal (earth) yields the sweet- flavoured milk, and thecloud-invested, undepressed heaven (yields) ambrosia, to those ─Аdityas whose strength is sacred praise, whoare bringers of rain, the doers of good actions, offer for your welfare laudation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whose strength is praise:ukthabal─Бn = very strong

Jamison Brereton

Those for whom their mother swells the honeyed milk, (for whom) Aditi, (like) unbounded heaven, massive as a stone, (swells) the beestings,
those whose gusts are hymns, bullishly bearing, rich in propertyтАФ
applaud those ─АdityasтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

I will rejoice in these Adityas for my weal, for whom the Mother pours forth water rich in balm,
And Dyaus the Infinite, firm as a rock, sweet milk,-Gods active, strong through lauds, whose might the Bull upholds.

Geldner

Denen die Mutter s├╝├Яe Milch quillt, die felsenfeste Himmels-Aditi ihren Rahm, die von Lobliedern ermutigten, Stierlasten tragenden, gut lohnenden, diese Aditya┬┤s begr├╝├Яe freudig zum Heile!

Grassmann

Sie, die die Mutter reichlich tr├дnkt mit s├╝ssem Trank, mit Milch der Himmel, unbegrenzt und felsenfest, Die spruchumrauschten, reichen, M├дnner hegenden Aditja’s will zum Heil begr├╝ssen jubelnd ich.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods, the never-slumbering beholders of mankind, and entitled (to their adoration), have obtainedgreat immortality; conveyed in chariots of light, possessed of unsurpassable wisdom, devoid of sin, they inhabitthe exalted station of heaven for the well-being (of the world).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having their eyes on men, unblinking, as their due the gods have
achieved lofty immortality.
Having light as their chariot, snake-sly, blameless, they wear the height of heaven as their garmentтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

Looking on men, ne’er slumbering, they by their deserts attained as Gods to lofty immortality.
Borne on refulgent cars, sinless, with serpents’ powers, they robe them, for our welfare, in the height of heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods, who, kings over all, and most exalted, have come to the sacrifice, who, unassailable, abidein heaven; them, the mighty ─Аdityas, (the sage) worships with reverence, and with praises, and also Aditi for hiswell- being.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The very strong sovereign kings who have come to the sacrifice, who, undeviating, have established their own dwelling in heavenтАФ
seek to entice them here with reverence, with well-turned (hymns)тАФthe great ─Аdityas and AditiтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

Great Kings who bless us, who have come to sacrifice, who, ne’er assailed, have set their mansion in the sky,-
These I invite with adoration and with hymns, mighty Adityas, Aditi, for happiness.

Grassmann

Die Herrscher, die dem Opfer segnend sind genaht, die unumst├╝rzbar thronen auf des Himmels Sitz, Die lock’ ich her durch Opferwerke und Gebet zum Heile die Aditja’s und die Aditi.

тАЬWho offers you the praise which you like, you wise universal deities, however many you may be?Deities from whom many are born, who can prepare for you such worship as may bear the safe beyond iniquityfor our well-being?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who brings to success for you the praise that you will enjoy, all you gods of Manu, however many you are?
Who will properly prepare for you, powerfully born ones, the ceremony that will carry us across difficult straitsтАФfor well-being?

Who, Mighty Ones, will prepare for you the sacrifice to bear us over trouble to felicity?

English translation:

тАЬ─Аdityas, to whom, Manu, having kindled the fire, offered the first sacrifice with (reverent) mind,(aided) by the seven ministrant priests, do you bestow upon us prosperity, free from peril; provide for us plural asantpaths easy to travel for our well-being.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You for whom Manu, with his fire kindled by mind, along with the seven Hotars, first attracted Hotr─Б (Libation) with sacrifice,
you ─Аdityas, hold out fearlessness as shelter. Make easy passages, easy pathways for usтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

Ye to whom Manu, by seven priests, with kindled fire, offered the first oblation with his heart and soul,
Vouchsafe us, ye Adityas, sheitcr free from fear, and make us good and easy paths to happiness.

Grassmann

Ihr, denen Manu weihte einst den ersten Guss, mit sieben Priestern willig bei des Feuers Glut, Ihr, o Aditja’s, reicht uns unbedrohten Schutz und bahnet sch├╢n die Pfade uns zum Wohlergehn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the wise and omniscient deities, who rule over the whole world both stationary and moveable,deliver us today from committed and uncommitted sin, for our well-being.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e., from actual bodily sin and frommental sin

Jamison Brereton

The forethoughtful counselors who are masters of the world, of everything stationary and movingтАФ
o gods, rescue us today from transgression done or not doneтАФfor
well-being.

Griffith

Wise Deities, who have dominion o’er the world, ye thinkers over all that moves not and that moves,
Save us from uncommitted and committed sin, preserve us from all sin to-day for happiness.

Geldner

Welche ├╝ber die ganze Welt vorausdenkend herrschen, ├╝ber alles was steht und geht als Sorger, ihr G├╢tter, sch├╝tzet uns heute vor getaner, vor ungetaner S├╝nde zum Heile!

Grassmann

English translation:

тАЬWe call in battles upon the well-invoked Indra, the liberator from sin, and upon the virtuous folk ofheaven, Agni, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, Bhaga, Heaven and Earth, the Maruts, for the acquisition (of food), for well-being.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In the raids we call on Indra easy to call, on the divine race of good action that releases from difficult straits,
on Agni, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, Bhaga, for winning, on Heaven and Earth, the MarutsтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

In battles we invoke Indra still swift to hear, and all the holy Host of Heaven who banish grief,
Agni, Mitra, and Varuna that we may gain, Dyays, Bhaga, Maruts, Prthivi for happiness:

English translation:

тАЬMay we for our well-being ascend the well-oared, defectless, unyielding, divine vessel, thesafe-sheltering expansive heaven, exempt from evil, replete with happiness, exalted and right-directing.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Allepithets, e.g. pс╣Ыthiv─лm are read with dy─Бm;

N─Бvam = n─Бvam iva; heaven is praised in the form of a ship; or,the cause of heaven

Jamison Brereton

Upon Earth of good protection and faultless Heaven, upon Aditi of good shelter, of good guidance,
(as) upon a divine boat with good oars, without defect, not leaking,
may we mountтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

Mightily-saving Earth, incomparable Heaven the good guide Aditi who gives secure defence
The well-oared heavenly Ship that lets no waters in, free from defect, will we ascend for happiness.

All you worthy of the sacrifice, speak for us, for help; rescue us from the crooked ill-going way.
With an invocation to the gods that comes true we would invoke you as you listen, o gods, for aidтАФfor well-being.

Bless us, all Holy Ones, that we may have your help, guard and protect us from malignant injury.
With fruitful invocation may we call on you, Gods, who give ear to us for grace, for happiness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Remove far) from us disease, remove all neglect of oblations, remove illiberality, the malevolence ofthose who wish to do us harm; remove far from us, gods, those who hate us; grant us ample happiness for ourwell-being.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Away with disease, away with all lack of oblation, away with the ill-met hostility of the malicious.
Gods, keep hatred at a distance from us. Extend broad shelter to usтАФ for well-being.

Griffith

Keep all disease afar and sordid sacrifice, keep off the wicked man’s malicious enmity.
Keep far away from us all hatred, O ye Gods, and give us ample shelter for our happiness.

тАЬUnharmed prospers every mortal, after performing his duties, he flourishes with posterity, whom you─Аdityas guide with good counsels safe over all misfortunes to well-being.тАЭ

Every mortal thrives unharmed and is propagated with progeny forth from his foundation,
whom, o ─Аdityas, you lead with your good leading across all difficult passagesтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

Untouched by any evil, every mortal thrives, and, following the Law, spreads in his progeny.
Whom ye with your good guidance, O Adityas, lead safely through all his pain and grief to happiness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The chariot) which, deities, you protect for the supply of food; that which, Maruts, (you protect) inbattle for the sake of the deposited spoil; may we mount, Indra, the early-moving desirable irresistible chariot forour well- being.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Which one, o gods, you help at the contest for prizes, which one, o Maruts, you help at the contest of champions when the stake is set,
that early-traveling, winning chariot, which suffers no harm, might we mount, o IndraтАФfor well-being.

Griffith

That which ye guard and grace in battle, O ye Gods, ye Maruts, where the prize is wealth, where heroes win,
That conquering Car, O Indra, that sets forth at dawn, that never breaks, may we ascend for happiness.

Geldner

Welchen Wagen ihr G├╢tter bevorzuget im Kampfe um den Siegerpreis, welchen ihr Marut beg├╝nstigt im Kampfe um den Tapfersten, wann der Preis ausgesetzt ist, den fr├╝hausfahrenden, gewinnbringenden, unbesch├дdigten Wagen m├╢chten wir, Indra, besteigen zum Heile!

Grassmann

Den Wagen, den, o G├╢tter, ihr im Krieg beeilt, und in der Schlacht, o Maruts, bei entbranntem Kampf, Der fr├╝he kommt, o Indra, und den Preis gewinnt, der nicht zerbricht, den lasst besteigen uns zum Heil.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, secure to us well-being on roads, in deserts, well-being in waters, midst the might of assailinghosts; well-being in the son-bearing wombs (of our wives); well-being for (the acquisition of) riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

On roas: indistricts fit for travelling, i.e., well-watered, as opposed to dhanvasu

Jamison Brereton

Well-being for us on the pathways and in the wastelands, well-being in the waters, in the precinct of the sun,
well-being for us in the wombs at the making of sonsтАФwell-being
confer (on us) for wealth, o Maruts.

Griffith

Vouchsafe us blessing in our paths and desert tracts, blessing in waters and in battle, for the light;
Blessing upon the wombs that bring male children forth, and blessing, O ye Maruts, for the gain of wealth.

Geldner

Gl├╝ck bringet uns auf den Wegen, auf dem Trocknen, Gl├╝ck zu Wasser, im Kampf, wo es um die Sonne geht, Gl├╝ck uns bei der Kinderzeugung im weiblichen Scho├Яe, Gl├╝ck bringet uns, ihr Marut, zum Reichtum!

Grassmann

Schafft Heil uns auf den Wegen, Heil uns auf dem Land, Heil auf dem Wasser, Heil im g├╝terreichen Sitz, Heil in den Sch├╢ssen bei der Kinderzeugung uns, und Heil, o Maruts, zu des reichen Guts Erwerb.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay (pс╣Ыthiv─л), who secures well-being to the excellent path, who, abounding with wealth, goes to thedesirable (plural ce of sacrifice), preserve our home, may she protect us on the path we have to travel; cherished bythe gods, may she be to us a plural asant abode.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For it is just well-being that is best on the path forwardтАФthat, (already) rich in inheritance, sets out toward something valuable.
Let it keep guard over us at home and in a foreign place; with the gods as its herdsmen let it be easy of access.

Griffith

The noblest Svasti with abundant riches, who comes to what is good by distant pathway,-
May she at home and far away preserve us, and dwell with us under the Gods’ protection

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUniversal deities and Aditi, thus has the prudent son of plural ti magnified you; the celestial people, theimmortal (company of the gods) through whom (when praised) men become the lords (of wealth) have beengloried by Gaya.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In just this way has the son of Plati of inspired thought strengthened you, all you ─Аdityas and Aditi.
The over-mastering superior men, the divine race, has been praised by Amartya Gaya.

Griffith

Thus hatb the thoughtful sage, the son of Plati, praised you, O Aditi and all Adityas,
Men are made rich by those who are Immortal: the Heavenly Folk have been extolled by Gaya.

Geldner

Also hat euch Plati┬┤s Sohn erbaut, ihr Aditya┬┤s alle, o Aditi, der Sinnreiche. Die m├дchtigen Herren und das himmlische Volk wurden von Amartya Gaya gepriesen.

Grassmann

So hat verherrlicht euch der Sohn des Plati, o weise Aditi, Aditja’s alle; Durch ew’ge G├╢tter werden stark die Menschen; durch Gaja ist ger├╝hmt das Volk des Himmels.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ-рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╣реЗ рд╕рдм рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯ рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдб рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди рдкрд░рдо рдЛрд╖рд┐рдпреЛрдВ ! (рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗ) рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдб рд╕реБрдЦрд╕рдореНрдкрддреНрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП (рд╡рдГ) рддреБрдореНрд╣реЗрдВ (рдкреНрд▓рддреЗрдГ рд╕реВрдиреБрдГ) рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХ (рдордиреАрд╖реА) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдЕрд╡реАрд╡реГрдзрддреН) рдмреЭрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рдИрд╢рд╛рдирд╛рд╕рдГ-рдирд░рдГ) рддреБрдо рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрдореБрдХреНрдд (рдЕрдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрди рдЧрдпреЗрди) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рдд рд╕рдм рдХреЗ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдиреЗ (рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ-рдЬрдирдГ) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдп рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп-рдЛрд╖рд┐ рдЬрди (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐) рд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рджреЗрдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезренрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдФрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рд╕реЗ рд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди, рд╕рдм рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдгрд╛рдд, рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрдореБрдХреНрдд, рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░ рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдФрд░ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди рдмрдирд╛рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЬреНрдЮ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдпрд╛ рдЙрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рд┐рдд рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдкрдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезренрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ-рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╣реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд┐рддрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдХрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рдорд░реНрд╖рдпрдГ (рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗ) рдЕрджрд┐рддрдпреЗ-рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд╕реБрдЦрд╕рдореНрдкрддреНрддрдпреЗ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╕рдореНрдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдкреНрд▓рддреЗрдГ рд╕реВрдиреБрдГ) рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддреБрд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп тАШрдкреНрд▓реБ рдЧрддреМтАЩ [рднреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐реж] тАШрддрддреЛ рдбрддрд┐рд░реНрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓рдХрд╛-рджреМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГтАЩ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ (рдордиреАрд╖реА) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд╡реАрд╡реГрдзрддреН) рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рддрд┐ (рдИрд╢рд╛рдирд╛рд╕рдГ-рдирд░рдГ) рдпреВрдпрдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреЛ рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрдореБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрди рдЧрдпреЗрди) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпреЗрдг рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ (рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ-рдЬрдирдГ) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ-рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ-рдЛрд╖рдпрдГ тАШрдПрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдВ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдиреЗтАЩ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐) рд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рджрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдГ реерезренрее
